Free Talk

A Laughing Matter 105

— Hai Ke

A—Recent newspapers have made much progress. In addition to many daily news items, there are also categories such as education and sports. But why do I often see an empty space?

B—Oh, that's because there's too much material. The characters are packed so tightly everywhere, so they deliberately open a window to let in some air.

Teacher—Children, we all know that the Earth is round, but you must provide me with three pieces of evidence to prove it.

Student—Sir, you said the Earth is round, my father also said the Earth is round, and my mother also said the Earth is round. Those are three pieces of evidence.

Girl A—What do you think Mr. D means? He comes to see me every night and is very affectionate with me.

Girl B—As I see it, perhaps it's because he loves you, or perhaps it's because he has no dinner at home.

A—I've recently embraced hedonism and want to be comfortable in every way, so I specially installed a bell on my bed the other day so I can ring it as soon as I open my eyes every morning.

B—In that case, how many servants do you employ at home?

A—All the housework is still done by my old mother. I just installed a bell.

Liu Weizhi Plans to Transform Model Railways 106

— Li Qingduo

Western countries have always valued transportation, and railway engineering is vast. A characteristic is that structures such as roofs and tunnels are built over railways, and trains run safely. The sophistication of their construction and the convenience of transportation are sufficient for our country to emulate. My country's railways currently only total more than 7,000 miles. Due to the influence of civil war and the lack of capital, their equipment is still relatively simple, and transportation is not entirely smooth. It is difficult to compare with Europe and the United States. However, looking at the national railways, the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou lines have been less affected by military affairs, so they are slightly better than other lines. The current director of the two railway administrations, Liu Weizhi, once studied in the United States and has long been engaged in railway affairs. Minister Sun of the Ministry of Railways appointed Liu as the director of the ministry's business department and concurrently oversaw the affairs of the two railway administrations. Since taking office, Liu has actively reorganized railway administration. In addition to handling routine official duties, he often takes time to browse books on railway construction and research various improvement plans, intending to use his strengths to turn the two lines into national model railways to serve as examples for other railways and increase the convenience of transportation in the capital. His plan is indeed very grand. Liu often told me about this, strongly emphasizing the necessity of transforming model railways and hoping to achieve his goals. Liu Juheng works diligently and rises early in the morning to go to the bureau on time. However, the Ministry of Railways is in Beijing, and the railway administration is in Shanghai. Liu must travel back and forth for official business, spending roughly half the week in Shanghai and half the week in Beijing. He travels frequently and spends two nights a week sleeping on the train, living his sleeping life on the train. Yet Liu shows no sign of fatigue, as he is accustomed to traveling and considers the distance between Beijing and Shanghai not far, taking the train as if taking a streetcar.

Strange Tales from Central Henan 107

— Qiushui

I have already published an article in this column about the suffering of the people in Central Henan. Now, I have heard that two monsters appeared in the southwest of Henan Province last month. The villagers believed they were divine messengers and were all panicked and did not know what to do. I will describe them below to show a glimpse of the recent situation of the people of Henan.

Nine Rats with One Tail: In the southwest of Henan Province, there is a small town. The person who mentioned it did not specify its name. A certain Mr. So-and-so in the town was sitting idly in the living room of his house one day when he suddenly felt something fall from the beam, hitting his foot. Mr. So-and-so was startled and looked at it, and it was a rat's nest. The young rats in the nest were wriggling, as if they were rats trying to escape after being shaken by the fall. Mr. So-and-so usually hated rats, so he stepped on the nest. The rats in the nest wailed incessantly, as if they could not bear the pain. Mr. So-and-so then lifted his foot, and the rats in the nest emerged. There were about five or six rats, staggering as they walked. Mr. So-and-so, being injured and unable to walk well, did not find it strange and then struck them with a club. All the rats died. Looking at them, there were six rats in total, but only one tail. The six rats were connected as one, so they moved clumsily. Mr. So-and-so was greatly shocked and told his neighbors. The neighbors came to watch and exclaimed in surprise. The elderly even took this as an ominous sign, saying that there would soon be a great flood or famine. For a time, the news spread far and wide, and everyone was anxiously thinking that disaster was about to strike, and they did not know what to do.

Dragon Head in Well: There are many wells in the countryside of Henan Province, and the residents rely on them for drinking water. There is often a pulley next to the well to draw water, so as to save time and effort. When the story of the nine rats with one tail was spreading among the people, suddenly a neighboring town also made a big commotion about a strange thing. A certain household in the town had a well and also used a pulley to draw water. One day, the owner went to the well to draw water and pulled the pulley by hand, but it would not move. Thinking that there was damage between the pulleys, he gathered his neighbors to pull it together, but it still would not move, and the pulley was unbearably heavy, as if something was holding it in the well. They could not help but look at each other in dismay. Everyone let go and waited for a change. The pulley then automatically drew water and splashed water from the well as if it were very high. After a long time, suddenly a strange head emerged from the well. Everyone shouted in fear, and the monster disappeared and could not be seen again. Everyone then told each other what they had seen, and everyone said in unison that it had horns, a beard, and yellow spots, and it was clearly a dragon's head.

A Person Well-Versed in the Three Principles of the People 108

— Tang Bihua

Yang Zhenqing from Xiaoshan graduated from higher primary school and is now employed in a certain silk shop in Hangzhou. He usually admires the revolution and worships President Sun. Since President Sun's death, he has mourned for three days and nights, almost neglecting food and sleep. He especially loves to read President Sun's posthumous work, the Three Principles of the People. Whenever the night is quiet and all sounds are still, he often holds a volume and silently recites it by the light, never missing an evening. Recently, he has become well-versed in the entire book and can recite it completely in two hours in one breath, which is quite pleasant to listen to. In his spare time, he often lectures on the Three Principles of the People, eloquently and tirelessly. Those who see him admire him without exception, and it is spread as a good story for a time.

Visiting Old Friends in Xuyuan 109

— Zheng Yimei

Butterflies are said to be transformed from the clothes left by Ge Hong, because they are light and ethereal among insects, wanting to become immortals and being naturally rich in literary talent. My predecessor, Tianxu Wusheng, had the surname Chen and the courtesy name Diexian, so he took the meaning of Zhuangzi's "fluttering butterfly" and named his residence Xuyuan. It is said that the old site of Xuyuan is in the south of Shanghai, but I have not been there. My younger brother Runsun moved with his mother from Qiaojia浜 in the south of the city to No. 1 Sanle Lane on Jingxiu Road in the West Gate. The lane is very short and secluded, with very few people passing by. My younger brother's residence is No. 1, facing south. There is also No. 2, facing west. There is no third house. I heard from my neighbor that this residence used to be a tooth powder factory. It was first in the No. 2 house, and then it moved to the No. 1 house. Now it has established a company and the business is very prosperous. I have always suspected that it was the birthplace of Tianxu Wusheng's industry, but I have not dared to confirm it. This Sunday, I entered the city to visit my mother. In the evening, I was taking a nap in front of the door when I suddenly saw a large brick embedded in the courtyard wall of the adjacent No. 2 house. The words "Xuyuan" were chiseled in large characters, with jade-like luster and roundness, and the calligraphy was perfect. Only then did I know that this was indeed the old residence of Tianxu Wusheng. It is a pity that the crude and ignorant have smeared and defaced the brick text, adding vulgar words such as "Prosperity to me." Thus, the wall is like a scab. My younger brother's residence is also where Tianxu Wusheng used to live and sing, which makes people imagine a family of elegant and artistic people.

Ricebird and Scarecrow 110

— Sun Linchang

Among birds, there are ricebirds that love to eat ripening rice grains. When it is the seventh month in the countryside, the leaves of the trees are slightly shed, and the new grains turn yellow. The long ears droop, and the sap condenses into grains. Then, hundreds of ricebirds gather in the fields, chirping and eating, happily spending their golden age. When people come to chase them away, they fly away, but when the people leave, they fly back and chirp. Therefore, the farmers suffer from it and can do nothing. Some people tie straw into a human shape to scare them. The scarecrow wears a straw hat, short clothes, and holds a long stick in its hand, looking like a farmer. Also, because it cannot stand upright, they insert a fishing rod into the field ridge and hang the scarecrow on the wheel hook, and under the scarecrow, they also hang two stones. When the ricebirds see it, they indeed think it is a person and dare not come. When I saw it, I laughed and thought it was just superficial work, and the swallows and sparrows would eventually be easily deceived. However, I did not know the intention of hanging two stones under the scarecrow, so I took away the two stones for them. Then, the west wind blew, and the scarecrow moved automatically, its clothes turned over, and the straw came out, revealing its true form. However, I did not pay attention to this at first. Then, ricebirds passed by and gathered at a distance to stare at it. After looking at it carefully for a long time, as if they realized that the scarecrow was fake, some of them gradually went down into the fields. After a while, those who came thought there was no danger, and those who had not come also gathered. Then the scarecrow's scare effect was completely lost. At this point, I realized that the reason for hanging two stones under the scarecrow was to prevent it from fluttering and showing its true form to people. From then on, the scarecrows in our village could no longer be relied on to intimidate ricebirds. Sometimes, ricebirds gathered on the scarecrow's body, chirping and fighting, and bird droppings fell like a group of people ridiculing the scarecrow. Ah, scarecrow!

Record of the Cricket 111

— He Tianjian

With one leaf falling in Dongting Lake, autumn returns to the earth, and autumn dominates killing. Those who obtain its energy are crickets. People use their fighting nature and take it as a recreational activity. They beautify its name as "Autumn Interest," which can also be said to be a good thing.

There are many kinds of crickets. Most ordinary ones are named according to their shape and color. However, their advantages and disadvantages, strength and weakness, also depend on the size of their shape and the difference in color. Often, an extremely ordinary shape and body can defeat those with extraordinary shapes and bodies. This cannot be distinguished without being old in this art and being a skilled appraiser. In my hometown, there is a certain Mr. Jia who keeps hundreds of crickets every autumn. Last autumn, he obtained an insect with a short and sharp body and a uniquely large head. At first, he did not think it was very special and despised it. After raising it for a long time and using it for fighting, it was surprisingly fierce and invincible. Half of the hundreds of insects he had were defeated by it. Before fighting, its antennae were straight and its appearance was very quiet. When fighting, its head and horns rose up, and its legs were like lances against the enemy. After being touched, it was repelled, its wings were broken, and it did not dare to face it. Mr. Jia did not know why it was like this at first. After several careful inspections, he realized that the reason for its victory was the strength of its head. So, he recognized it as a hero and placed it in an expensive container and carefully fed it, calling it "Locomotive" to symbolize its sharpness and ferocity. However, because of its body weight, it was difficult to find a match for it when choosing a partner. Mr. Jia used it in fighting matches and often used it to fight against insects that were twice its weight, even insects that were three times as large. In this battle, at the beginning of the fight between the two insects, the Locomotive was thrown onto the fence top because its strength was not enough. Everyone thought it would definitely lose, but unexpectedly, in the blink of an eye, the one three times its weight suddenly fell into the fence gap, and the one shouting wildly was the Locomotive. It turns out that after the Locomotive was thrown out, the other one was about to stretch its legs and rub its antennae to show its victory. The Locomotive took the opportunity to jump into its abdomen, attacking its weakness, and used its head and horns to hit its tail, causing it to be thrown out. This can be said to be good at using intelligence. The enemy then stroked its antennae again to try to decide the outcome again, but the insect had its legs suppressed and its tail damaged and could not fight. Then the victory was decided. It was heard that the Locomotive was obtained under a mulberry root. When Mr. Jia caught it, he first encountered a red snake and thought it had moved elsewhere. When he passed by the place again, the sound was still there. He poured water into it and then obtained it. It can also be said to be a miracle. Mr. Jia relied on it to make several thousand dollars, because it was invincible and always won. Later, it was heard that it was resold to someone in Jiangyin, and the price was 2,000 gold coins.

Travels in Southeast Asia (49) 112

— Linghua

The car arrived at the Guan Yin Temple in Kuala Lumpur. Next to it was the Chen Clan Ancestral Hall, which was large in scale. It is common for people overseas to organize themselves by clan to enhance their family's reputation. This practice is most prevalent in Guangdong, but it is especially necessary overseas. It is feared that as methods of collective organization progress, there may be gradual changes. The method of forming groups and the visit to the Jingwu Athletic Association for men included various Chinese and Western musical instruments, various weapons, and affiliated schools and newspaper reading rooms.

An employee, Mr. Huang, was asked whether Westerners were members of Jingwu. He replied that due to the issue of ethnicity, foreigners were not allowed to learn our martial arts. We also visited the women's section. The director, Ms. Feng, has been here for nine years. The new building is far superior to the one in Singapore, being spacious and grand. Outside the gate, the bamboo forest is well-maintained. Ms. Feng asked me about Kunhua. I replied that the suffering of human reproduction is entirely borne by mothers, while males use it to go shooting. In the future, women around the world should unite. If males want to start a major war, it must be approved by women around the world who are wives and mothers. This is one way to correct the practice of war. On that day, it was a holiday and all the agencies were closed, and no one could be visited. It is said that Kuala Lumpur is the center of the four states of Selangor. Among the hundreds of thousands of Chinese, there are two middle schools, one is Zun Kong and the other is Kun Cheng. There are many primary schools and dozens of groups. There are Guangxi provincial groups, which are not found in Singapore.

I took the train to Baling. The train seemed low, not as good as the Chinese trains. A third-class ticket to Ba Shuang Harbor cost four jiao per person. Workers sold food next to the train, and there were also Chinese people selling Shanghai's Liangyou magazine. The ship returned at 2 o'clock, and the passengers boarded after 4 o'clock. There were many Malays and Indians, filling the deck, but I was the only one in second class. It was hot, so the breeze on the deck was cool. But I felt that the problem of bread was secondary in Southeast Asia, and the first was showering to reduce body heat. Therefore, I sat in second class to be able to shower freely. This proves that those who believe in Marx's idea that bread is the only problem in life are wrong.

Warmth in the Heart (277) 113

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter 14: Emerald Bamboo Tears Stain, Beauty's Heart is Broken; Red Lotus Fragrance Fades, Maiden's Soul Departs

Using the name of doing business and socializing with friends to engage in the business of seeking pleasure is a major topic for those in Shanghai who frequent prostitutes. It seems that this business cannot be done without eating, drinking, and whoring. Generally, they hold this kind of excuse for their own spouses, whether it is their principal wife, concubine, or temporary mistress. Their female counterparts also know the economic principle that the source of financial income relies entirely on the head of the household. In order for him to earn money to support the family's extravagant spending, they naturally have to be lenient with him. Therefore, that woman, Zhang Yiqing, does not prohibit him from whoring, but the three chapters of the agreement have already been stipulated. His notice is similar to the Shanghai Municipal Council banning theaters and playgrounds, only effective until 12 o'clock at night. He must check in before 12 o'clock. Although his wife's 12 o'clock is like the 12 o'clock in the daytime of ordinary people, which is the center of the day, because she is treating liver pain and has become addicted to opium, she gets up at six or seven o'clock every evening and only goes to sleep when it is almost dawn. It doesn't matter if their master returns a little later, but she seems to be under strict marital guidance and must have a rule. Zhang Yiqing ultimately feels that this rule restricts people's freedom too much. To struggle in this harsh rule, the only way is to use the "teasing" method. Sometimes she says she has gone somewhere, sometimes she is held back by friends. By this, she can be pardoned for one night or two nights. Only after he obtained the good job of comprador of the Yangtze River steamboat could it be said that he had obtained liberation and freedom. He said that according to the company's regulations, all senior compradores must travel with the ship at least once a month. As for junior compradores, it is even more necessary to travel. Since he has become a senior comprador, he cannot but obey the company's regulations. His wife has no choice but to let him do so. He also brings back some Yunnan, Guizhou, and Sichuan specialties every time to please her. Therefore, at first, Hankou was his hunting ground, and then gradually he was liberated to Shanghai. At home, he only says that the comprador has boarded the ship and the ship has already sailed. In fact, he doesn't know that he is hiding in a small house somewhere. That house may be smaller than a ship. All the Yunnan, Guizhou, and Sichuan specialties can be brought back by others. Even if the comprador doesn't board the ship, the benefits can still be distributed. Therefore, he has the courage to take Cuiyun as a concubine. Fortunately, the people who accompany him are all helping him, and some people have been instructed in advance. Originally, his matter of occupying a friend's wife was not public among many fellow villagers, but more than half of them already knew about it. However, everyone has their own secrets and their own ulterior motives. No one will expose anyone else. Some people even have requests for him, so they naturally help him say good things.

Municipal Propaganda Department's Statement Regarding the Price Increase of Water in the Foreign Concessions 114

The Municipal Propaganda Department issued a statement to the public regarding the unprovoked price increase of tap water in the Public Concession, stating: "Tap water is one of the public utilities. Therefore, in European and American countries, these public utilities are all operated by the state, and the prices charged to users are very low. The purpose is to facilitate the citizens rather than to make profits. Since the opening of China to foreign trade, we have been bound by the unequal treaties of various imperialist countries. Our country has no say in all the administrative matters within the concessions. As for the recent forced price increase by the Shanghai Waterworks Company, the Municipal Council, which bears the administrative responsibility for the concession, approved it in disregard of the people's livelihood. From this one incident, it can be seen that their collusion is truly outrageous. Moreover, the price of tap water in the concession was originally calculated based on 6% of the house price. In recent years, house prices in Shanghai have risen year by year, and the company's income has increased invisibly a lot. Now there is even an increase to 25%, an unreasonable oppression that is intolerable. At this time of difficult living, all our citizens must unite and oppose the price increase. We vow not to pay until the goal is achieved. On the one hand, we must recognize that imperialists oppress our people in every possible way. In order to seek the root cause, we must unite to assist the government to recover the concessions in the shortest possible time. I hope you will take these matters into consideration."

Continuing to Request the Collection of Fees for Dredging Yutang 117

The Yutang Dredging Preparatory Committee submitted a document to the Shanghai County Government and the Construction Bureau yesterday, stating: "We respectfully report that the funds required for dredging Yutang have been resolved by the council through land tax collection. Instruction No. 6 from your bureau stated that the request for land tax collection was approved. However, the area of tax collection and the amount of tax collection per mu were not stated in detail, which seemed vague. A detailed response should be provided before further review. This order, etc., was received. In the midst of handling this, we received Instruction No. 290 from your government, which stated that the case had been submitted to the 34th county government meeting for discussion and it was decided that if the land tax collection exceeded the limit, the local people should devise other methods and prepare a detailed budget to be submitted to the county for review and filing. We should comply with this order. This order, etc., was received. We then submitted it to the 7th preparatory meeting for discussion and resolved that the dredging of the river was a profit-generating undertaking and was different from the nature of ordinary mu donations. Moreover, the burden was only on the farmers on both banks of Yutang who were related to water conservancy and not on all the people in the county uniformly. Moreover, the funds were a temporary levy, so we should not abandon the effort because of the provincial quota. The council should prepare a budget and continue to request review, etc. We then discussed how to stipulate the method of tax collection and decided to collect in two installments. The first installment was to collect 1 jiao per mu in the winter rice tax of the 19th year. The second installment was to collect 5 fen in the busy season silver tax of the 20th year, etc. It is on file that Yutang is a major transportation river connecting Songjiang and Shanghai counties, extending 27 li from east to west. The commerce and transportation of the three towns of Beitang and Matang rely on this river. The irrigation of farmland along the river reaches more than 54,000 mu. Recently, due to years of disrepair, it has become increasingly silted up, and the irrigation of farmland will be cut off, and the transportation of boats will be hindered. This is the biggest reason for the decline in agricultural production and the depression of commerce. At this time of political training and construction, increasing production and developing people's livelihood are the biggest tasks of local self-government agencies. The council, in view of this, collected the opinions of local people and adapted to the needs of farmers along the river. Although it knew that the land tax collection exceeded the limit, it was permissible for the farmers to endure the pain for a time to reap endless benefits. It seems that we do not need to stick to it. Moreover, the tax collection is only limited to the farmland on both banks along the river, not all the people in the county uniformly bear it. The public unanimously agreed. It is reasonable to prepare a detailed budget and the method of tax collection and submit them to your superiors for review and approval. We respectfully request that your superiors review and quickly forward them to the Jiangsu Provincial Construction Department for approval to collect taxes to benefit river works and increase agricultural production."

Municipal Finance Bureau: Financial Discussion Meeting to be Established 118

The Rules Have Been Approved by the Municipal Government

The Municipal Finance Bureau is preparing to establish a financial discussion committee to vigorously improve the city's finances. It is now learned that the rules for the financial discussion committee formulated by the bureau have been submitted to the municipal government and approved as proposed. Official letters have been prepared to invite economic and financial experts and famous figures from the financial community in Shanghai to serve as members of the committee. It is said that the committee will be established soon. The rules of the committee are excerpted as follows: (Article 1) The Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau (hereinafter referred to as the Bureau) has established the Financial Discussion Committee (hereinafter referred to as the Committee) in order to gather ideas and work hard to improve and develop the city's finances. (Article 2) The Committee shall consist of 21 members, who shall be appointed by the Director of the Bureau from financial and economic experts or those with rich financial experience. (Article 3) The Chairman and Vice Chairman of the Committee shall be elected by the members. (Article 4) The tasks of the Committee are as follows: 1. Matters concerning the city's financial planning; 2. Matters concerning the city's financial review; 3. Matters concerning the city's financial implementation and assistance. (Article 5) The matters in the preceding article shall be proposed by the Director of the Bureau or the members, and after being decided by the Committee, shall be submitted by the Director to the Mayor for approval. (Article 6) In addition to the Director of the Bureau, more than half of the members must be present at the Committee meeting to hold a meeting. The meeting must be approved by more than half of the members present to obtain a vote. (Article 7) If a member is unable to attend due to an event, he may entrust another member to represent him by letter, but only one member may be represented at the same time. (Article 8) The Committee shall hold one meeting per month, which shall be convened by the Chairman. When necessary, the Bureau may consult with the Chairman to convene an extraordinary meeting. The Chairman shall notify the members of the date and time of each meeting and the matters to be discussed two days in advance. (Article 9) The Committee shall set up the following groups. If there is a motion, the nature may be distinguished and submitted to the relevant group for review, or reviewed jointly by two or more groups. All members must independently identify one or two groups to take charge of review matters: 1. Financial Administration Group; 2. Economic Group; 3. Tax Group; 4. Accounting Group; 5. Municipal Property Group; 6. Public Debt Group. (Article 10) The Committee shall set up two to three clerks to handle documents and general affairs, who shall be concurrently filled by staff of the Bureau. (Article 11) All members of the Committee shall be unpaid. (Article 12) The detailed rules for the Committee's affairs shall be formulated separately. (Article 13) These rules shall be implemented from the date of approval by the Municipal Government. If there are any matters that are not exhaustive, they may be decided by the Committee, revised, and submitted to the Municipal Government for approval.

Disappointment Regarding Autumn Cocoons in Jiangsu and Zhejiang 119

Significant Losses for the Silk Industry

This year, the estimated yield of autumn cocoons in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces was expected to be around 60,000 piculs. Unexpectedly, due to weather conditions, the harvest has been greatly disappointing, and the quality is extremely poor. Wuxi has already started weighing the cocoons, and the worst quality requires 3,600 to 3,700 catties of fresh cocoons to produce 100 catties of silk. Even the best quality cocoons require more than 2,700 catties. Silk factories in Shanghai that had not yet set out to purchase autumn cocoons are now canceling their rental agreements with cocoon farmers. The farmers, aware of the poor quality, are eager to sell their cocoons even at a reduced price of 20 to 30 yuan per picul, but manufacturers are hesitant to buy. A silk merchant in Xiyi (Wuxi) bought them at 20 yuan per picul to test the silk reeling, but the result was also a loss, so he has stopped purchasing. Xiejiao in Zhejiang opened its weighing scales the other day with an initial price of 55 yuan per picul. Seeing that 800 to 900 catties were required for silk reeling, the price dropped to 40 yuan, but there are still concerns about maintaining the market. As for cocoons in areas such as Linping in Hangzhou, they also require more than 830 catties for silk reeling. Silk factories are eager to cancel their rental agreements to avoid further losses. Purchasers in areas like Changan are hesitant and cautious about opening their scales. Overall, this year's silk cocoon situation in China is such that the shortage of raw materials in the spring and summer led to soaring cocoon prices. This was simultaneously affected by the price drops in Japanese silk and the stagnation of sales in the American market, causing significant losses for all silk factories. They had hoped for a bountiful autumn cocoon harvest to make up for the losses, but the outcome is the opposite. Therefore, all manufacturers are sighing and frowning in despair.

Brief Biography of Mr. Dragon, the New Danish Consul 120

The "Zi Lin Bao" reports that the newly appointed Danish Consul-General in Shanghai, Mr. Dragon, arrived in Shanghai last week to assume his post. Mr. Dragon is a veteran diplomat who has been stationed in various countries for a long time. Before coming to Shanghai from Sydney, he served as the Consul-General for Australia and New Zealand for eight years. Prior to that, he was the Consul in San Francisco, and even earlier, he was stationed in the capital of Norway for nine years. After leaving his post in Australia, he traveled extensively in the Dutch East Indies before coming to his new post in Shanghai.

Labor's Conditions in the Sino-Japanese Labor Dispute 123

The strike at the Sino-Japanese cotton mill in Pudong has been ongoing for a long time. The Social Affairs Bureau convened both labor and management representatives for mediation the other day (the 12th), but the management's attitude was tough, and no resolution was reached. Labor convened a general meeting of all workers yesterday morning to discuss the matter. As a result, they decided to demand that management accept the following five minimum conditions in preparation for negotiations: 1. Wages for the strike period will be paid to each person for two weeks. 2. Monthly bonus will be increased from two credits to four credits. 3. Rice allowance for two months during the strike period will be paid, a total of sixteen dimes. 4. The seven dismissed workers will be reinstated as usual. 5. The four factory stooges will be dismissed.

Committee to Revise the Constitution of the Red Cross 127

Continues to Meet

The Chinese Red Cross Constitution Revision Committee continued its meeting at 2:00 PM on September 13th. The attendees were Li Zhenbang, Wen Lanting, Xu Xichun, Jiang Daqiu, Dong Xinqin, Wang Peiyuan, Yang Ke, Wu Jiasan, Ye Zhisheng, Wang Xiaolai, Xue Shaoting, Liu Hongsheng, Hong Yanbin, and other committee members. Chairman Wen Lanting presided over the meeting, and Secretary Wei Ruifeng recorded the minutes. The agenda from the previous meeting was read, and the attendees had no objections. The chairman signed the minutes. (1) The chairman reported that today's third reading of the election law for Standing Council members. According to Committee Member Ye Daqiu, the election law still has many aspects that need to be revised. It is appropriate to conduct a thorough study of the matter. Therefore, today's third reading is changed to a discussion, and the third reading will be postponed to the next meeting. (1) Committee Member Dong Xinqin proposed, and Committee Member Jiang Daqiu seconded, that the name of the election law should be changed to the "Election Law of the Red Cross Society of the Republic of China" and that the chapters should be changed to: Chapter 1: General Provisions, Chapter 2: Election Law for National Members' Congress Representatives, Chapter 3: Election Law for Standing Council Members. (1) Committee Member Dong Xinqin proposed that two items should be added to Article 1: 1. Election of representatives to the National Members' Congress 2. Election Law for Standing Council Members. (1) Committee Member Jiang Daqiu proposed that all articles should be moved. The original Article 12 is changed to Chapter 2, Article 2. The article is changed to: Members belonging to the General Association shall use the General Association as the electoral district; members belonging to the branch association shall use the location of each branch association as the electoral district. The original Article 9 is changed to Article 3. The phrase "all members listed above may attend as representatives" is deleted, and the phrase "that is, they have the right to elect to be Standing Council members" is changed to "that is, they have the right to be elected to attend as representatives." The original Article 14 is changed to Article 4. The committee agreed to change the wording to: The number of representatives is specified as follows: (1) One representative for each branch association with 30 or more members; (2) Two representatives for each branch association with 50 to 100 members; (3) Three representatives for each branch association with 100 to 200 members; (4) Four representatives for each branch association with 200 to 500 members; (5) Five representatives for each branch association with 500 or more members, but no more than five representatives. The original Article 15 is changed to Article 5. The committee agreed that the phrase "the General Association shall notify each member at the same time" should be changed to "the General Association shall notify each member in the location at the same time." The section "The General Association organizes the Members' Congress" should be listed as a separate article. The original Article 10 is changed to Article 6, Article 17 is changed to Article 7, and Article 18 is changed to Article 8, and the wording is changed to: "Representative election tickets shall use the named continuous election method." The original Article 19 is changed to Article 9, and the committee agreed to change the wording to: "After receiving the election tickets from the General Association, the branch association shall select a date to convene a members' congress to hold the election ceremony, which shall be supervised by the speaker and deputy speaker, and the chairman and vice-chairman." The original Article 20 is changed to Article 10. The committee agreed to change the wording to: "Elected representatives shall be elected according to the number of seats, with those who receive the most votes being the elected candidates. After the election, each branch association shall submit the details of the process along with the election tickets to the General Association." The original Article 21 is changed to Article 11, Article 22 is changed to Article 12, Article 23 is changed to Article 13, and Article 24 is changed to Article 14. Committee Member Yang Ke proposed that the wording should be changed to: "The General Association shall pay for the board and lodging expenses of the representatives attending the National Members' Congress during the congress period, and the amount shall be determined temporarily by the Standing Council." The original Article 25 is changed to Article 15. The original Article 26 is changed to Article 16, and the wording is changed to: "The election of Standing Council members shall be conducted in the location of the General Association." Article 20 is changed to Article 18. The committee agreed to change the wording to: "The elected Standing Council members are not limited to attending representatives. Honorary members, special members, and regular members who are citizens of the Republic of China, are at least 25 years old, and have been members for more than two years may be elected as Standing Council members, but they must reside in Shanghai permanently after being elected to avoid absence." The original Articles 28, 29, and 30 are all deleted. The original Article 31 is changed to Article 19. Committee Member Wu Jiasan proposed that the number of Standing Council members should be appropriately increased. Chairman and Committee Member Li Zhenbang seconded. The committee agreed to change it to 51 members. The original Article 32 is changed to Article 20, Articles 33 and 34 are deleted and changed. The original Article 35 is changed to Article 21. Committee Member Yang Ke said that the word "persuade" should be changed to "campaign." Article 36 is changed to Article 22, and Article 37 is changed to Article 23. The committee agreed to change the wording to: "Standing Council member election tickets shall use the named continuous election method. Each representative shall be issued a numbered election ticket booklet, with 51 tickets in each booklet, and each ticket shall be filled out in ink to be valid." The original Article 38 is changed to Article 24. The original Article 28 is changed to Article 25, and Article 29 is changed to Article 26. (1) The chairman stated that today's third reading of the election law has been changed to a discussion. The third reading of the election law will continue next Monday (September 15th). If there is time, the third reading of the branch association's general rules will also be discussed. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM.

Yesterday's Disturbance at the Shandong Guild Hall 130

Shanghai has always been a gathering place for merchants and people from all provinces. Generally, each province has established public offices and guild halls to unite regional friendships and handle public welfare and charitable undertakings. Yesterday afternoon, about six to seven hundred Shandong merchants and business people gathered at the Shandong Guild Hall on Ximen Road in the French Concession. They questioned the guild committee members, including Jiang, Li, and Zhang, about why the credit directory had not been published for the past two years. Due to personal disputes, the guild had repeatedly been involved in lawsuits and had arbitrarily misused public funds. This time, Shandong merchants and business people intended to borrow space from the guild hall for charitable activities such as providing materials and medicine, but they were rejected by the committee members. It seems that such a large public guild hall is controlled by a few committee members. Therefore, they jointly raised questions. The two sides argued and there was some disturbance.

Hu Lianquan of Chuanshan Township Initiates the Construction of the Chuanshan Guild Hall 131

Chuanshan Town, which belongs to Zhenhai County in Zhejiang Province, is the main gateway for Yan, Tai, and Hai townships of the county, as well as Xie South and Xie North townships of Dinghai County. Tens of thousands of Chuanshan natives reside in Shanghai, many of whom are prominent businessmen. In the past, Chuanshan natives returning to their hometown had to detour through Ningbo. Even coffins of the deceased had to be transported from Shanghai to Ningbo and then collected by the Siming Public Office in Ningbo for return to Chuanshan. However, this process took a year, and if the family of the deceased did not claim the coffin within the time limit, the public office would rebury it in the Yishan cemetery, which was extremely inconvenient. Since the establishment of direct shipping between Shanghai and Chuanshan, transportation has become more convenient, eliminating the need to detour through Ningbo. However, the transportation of coffins still followed the previous practice. Hu Lianquan, a native of Chuanshan residing in Shanghai, witnessed this situation and initiated the construction of the Chuanshan Guild Hall to allow the families of poor Chuanshan natives in Shanghai to directly transport coffins back to their hometown, which would be both convenient and cost-saving. However, this matter is significant, and Mr. Hu believes that it cannot be accomplished without the collective effort of everyone. Therefore, he drafted a plan and sent a letter to the Ningbo Shanghai Native Place Association for assistance. After receiving the letter, the association invited Mr. Hu to the association at 10:00 AM yesterday to discuss the way forward. It is reported that the discussion was very satisfactory. The association will organize a meeting of Chuanshan natives this Sunday (September 21st) to discuss the plans. It is expected that the Chuanshan natives will care about their hometown and will not hesitate to contribute to the success of the project to benefit the poor natives in the transportation and storage of coffins.

Our association, concerned about our hometown, cannot remain silent. We urgently request Your Excellency to quickly dispatch a large army to suppress the bandits to quell the unrest and reassure the people. The Danyang Shanghai Native Place Association, with urgent anticipation."

Two Lost Boys Awaiting Collection 134

The Municipal Public Security Bureau received a lost boy named Fu Sanlou from the Second Precinct of the Fourth District. It is said that he is nine years old and from Xinghua County. His father's name is Fu Jinmao, and he and his elder brother, Yongyi, were farming in their hometown. Later, due to financial difficulties, they came to Shanghai to pull rickshaws for a living. His mother and sister-in-law work in a Huzhou silk factory. He does not know the name of the street, alley, or house number of his house because he was out playing and got lost on Hengfeng Road. He was found by the police and sent to the bureau. The boy has a sallow complexion and yellow skin. He has short hair on his forehead. He is wearing a blue cloth shirt and trousers and is barefoot in blue cloth shoes. He is now sent to the Women and Children Relief Association to be cared for and await collection.

Also, a mute lost boy was sent from the Fifth Precinct of the Fifth District. The police found a mute lost boy at the intersection of Yongyi Lane in Jiangwan and sent him to the bureau. The boy is mute and about twelve or thirteen years old. He has a monk's haircut, a rectangular face, and a sunken nose. His left thumb is disabled and cannot be bent. He is wearing a gray crepe adult's torn cotton-padded jacket with a white cloth undershirt.

He is wearing blue open-crotch trousers and is barefoot without shoes or socks. He is now sent to the Puyutang orphanage to be cared for and await collection.

Dahua Factory Submits Proposal to Adopt National Woolen Fabrics 136

The Dahua Factory submitted a document to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce and the Ministry of Education stating: "We are submitting a proposal to promote the use of domestically produced woolen fabrics and serge. Recently, with gold becoming more valuable and silver becoming cheaper, the price of all imported daily necessities has increased several times, further impoverishing the people. Therefore, those with aspirations are competing to promote national products and promote industry, which is fundamental to the national economy and the people's livelihood. Our factory is also a member of the nation, and our patriotism is always at the forefront. Therefore, we have always been meticulous in research and diligent in management. We have organized the Dahua Woolen and Linen Factory to purchase the latest machinery to produce various serge and linen for making ceremonial clothes and casual wear. In this time of rising prices and declining people's livelihood, we are especially willing to do our best to meet the needs of society and not consider personal interests. However, the people are either accustomed to extravagance or limited by their knowledge, and even if there are good domestic products, they do not know to use them, causing money to flow out of the country, weakening the country and impoverishing the people. Thinking of this, we can only sigh. We believe that the late Premier's Principle of People's Livelihood is to revitalize industry and encourage domestic products to cultivate the wealth and strength of the country. The Ministries adhere to the late Premier's teachings and take into account the current difficulties, and will certainly be happy to promote anything that can benefit the country and the people. Therefore, if domestic woolen and linen serge are used for official and private clothing to set an example, the influence from above will be swift, and a patriotic spirit will be cultivated and promoted, which will have a significant effect. Furthermore, the Ministry of Military Affairs has recently purchased a large quantity of woolen materials to make military uniforms and has used as much of our factory's products as possible. Therefore, we boldly submit samples for your inspection and request that you promote and encourage their use, and order all offices and national institutions to uniformly use domestic woolen and linen serge to make official and private clothing. Not only will this be our private wish, but it will also benefit the national economy and the people's livelihood. Respectfully submitted to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce and the Ministry of Education."

Three Missing Persons 137

Chen Dachen: At around 5:00 PM the other day, a man named Chen Peiqing reported to the water police that his younger brother, Chen Dachen, 22 years old from Anhui, had suddenly disappeared for no reason at around 9:00 PM on the eleventh of this month and had not returned. He feared that his brother, burdened by secret grief, had committed suicide in the Huangpu River. Therefore, he requested that the police be instructed to pay attention. The clothes he was wearing were a gray patterned serge long gown, a white silk short gown, a hemp gauze checkered short trousers, white socks, and black leather shoes. The police chief approved the request and instructed the detectives to pay attention.

Cui: Cui, an elderly woman from Hubei, 53 years old, is currently working as a maid in a swallow's nest in a lane under the Dongxin Bridge in the French Concession. On the morning of the twelfth, the owner of the swallow's nest suddenly accused Cui of stealing several opium bubbles, which led to a quarrel. Cui was extremely frustrated and suddenly disappeared. The owner of the swallow's nest was greatly alarmed and told Cui's son, Mingjin, to send people to search everywhere, but she was still nowhere to be found. Cui's son feared that she had committed suicide in the Huangpu River in a fit of anger. Therefore, at 6:00 PM the other day, he reported to the water police to pay attention.

Yinlong: Yinlong, a 22-year-old native of Pudong, was the head of the pier ship on the outer barrier of the Qiuxin Steamer, which was moored at the French Company Pier at around 8:00 PM the other night. At that time, he went to the steamer to take a bath and suddenly disappeared. He could not be found anywhere. The owner of the ship feared that he had accidentally fallen into the Huangpu River and died. Therefore, he reported to the water police yesterday to search for the body.

Discovery of Reefs Between Da Chen Shan Islands 140

Sea Customs Marine Affairs Section Inspectorate Notice: This Inspectorate, after investigating the waters within the jurisdiction of the Wenzhou Customs Tax Office, discovered reefs between the Da Chen Shan Islands. The details and estimated position of the reefs are listed below: A section of reefs, previously unrecorded on nautical charts, was found near the anchorage between the Da Chen Shan Islands of Taizhou. At low tide, the water depth above the reef is ten feet. The location of the reef is as follows: Latitude 28 degrees 27 minutes 48 seconds North, Longitude 121 degrees 51 minutes 30 seconds East (See British Admiralty Chart No. 1759). Therefore, all vessels are hereby notified to pay close attention and record this information carefully to avoid accidents. Be sure to take heed. This notice is issued on September 4th, Republic of China Year 19.

Strange Japanese Youth 146

Swallows Snakes and Eats Live Chickens

Hosted by the Shanghai Daily News

Usually Eats Bark, Rats, Frogs, and Flies

Strange Habits of Mountain Dwellers

New Research in Physiology

The strange youth, Sato Tomiji, is from Yamagata Prefecture, Japan. He is currently 27 years old. He lost his mother at a young age and was supported by his uncle, but eventually, he grew tired of it and left to live in the mountains. Initially, he ate grass, trees, and leaves, but then he began to enjoy snakes, rats, and frogs. Over time, it became a habit and he became different from ordinary people. Years ago, he traveled to Taiwan, Korea, and Manchuria. On July 9th of this year, he arrived in Dalian and praised the Dalian leaves as sweeter and more delicious than those in other places. At that time, local people were surprised and hospitals conducted research, causing a sensation. On the 12th of this month, he arrived in Shanghai on the Shanghai Maru and stayed at the Yachiyo Hotel on Wusong Road. He told people about it, and many were skeptical. The next day, the Shanghai Daily News gathered dozens of people and invited him to the auditorium. He devoured a live snake and a chicken in front of everyone. He held the snake's head and tail with both hands and bit it in the middle, discarding the tail and eating to the head. He first broke the neck of the live chicken and drank its blood, then ate the meat. Everyone was amazed. The next day, the reporter encountered Mr. Sato on the street and bought thirteen snakes as food. In the morning, he caught flies for breakfast when he was hungry. This is also sufficient for new research in physiology.

Posing as Veterans to Solicit Donations for Wounded Soldiers 147

The Scheme Exposed

Four People Apprehended

For days, individuals resembling discharged soldiers in groups of three to five have been appearing at the Qichang Pier and along the Huangpu River in Pudong. They solicit donations from people, claiming that a large number of wounded soldiers from the front lines will soon be transported back to Shanghai and housed in the Yu Jia Temple in Pudong. However, a large sum of money is needed to accommodate them. They claim to have been ordered by their superiors to solicit donations from philanthropists so that arrangements can be made in advance. Otherwise, there will inevitably be trouble in the area. The shipping agents and foremen at the piers, moved by their eloquent words, readily donated several or more than ten dollars and gave the solicitors a business card of the "Commander Li Qingsheng" as a receipt. Yesterday morning at 8 AM, they went to the pier to solicit donations again. Someone noticed the loophole and secretly reported it to the Third Team of the Qichang Pier Yangjing District Defense Corps. Team members were dispatched to investigate. When they realized they were exposed, they fled west. Four people were apprehended near Lujiadu and brought to the Corps headquarters before being sent to the Third District of the Public Security Bureau. One of them, Chen Jingbiao, 32 years old, from Xushuguan, Suzhou, stated that he was formerly a first-class soldier in the Eleventh Company, Third Battalion, Eighteenth Regiment, Ninth Brigade, Third Division. He was discharged this March and came to Shanghai without anything to do. Driven by poverty, he asked his friends to solicit assistance at the pier last night and received thirty to forty dollars in total. He got more than ten dollars. Another, Jiang Asheng, 28 years old, from Yuyao, stated that he was formerly a soldier in the Fifth Company, Second Battalion, Sixty-sixth Regiment, Thirty-third Brigade, Eleventh Division. He was wounded in the head by gunfire and was treated at the Eighteenth Rear Hospital. Now that his wound has healed, he came to Shanghai to look for friends. He met Chen Jingbiao at the pier and discussed the plan. He only received three or four dollars. Another, Wu Xiguo, 24 years old, from Changzhou, was formerly a soldier in the Eleventh Company, Third Battalion, Eighteenth Regiment, Ninth Brigade, Third Division. Another, Liu Rensheng, 29 years old, from Wuxi, was in the same company as Wu Xiguo. The rest of his statement was similar to Chen Jingbiao's. Six dollars in cash, four diaries, a discharge certificate, a ship's pass, fifteen business cards of Li Qingsheng, three symbols, and two Ning Shao ferry tickets were found on Chen and the others. The district chief, believing that the soldiers had violated the law by falsely soliciting donations, sentenced them to be escorted to the General Bureau in the afternoon for verification and handling.

American Female Traveler Walker Arrives in Shanghai 149

The Ambition to Walk Around the World Alone

Walking around the world has become commonplace in recent years, but it is still rare for women. Ms. Walker of the United States has a great spirit of intrepidity and intends to walk around the world alone with a bag. She recently arrived in Shanghai from Hong Kong. Ms. Walker started from Toronto, Canada,

Embarked on a walking tour through the Atlantic coastal states of the United States and arrived in Havana, Cuba. Afterwards, she went to Mexico, turned north through the Pacific coast to Alaska and returned south, crossing the sea to Honolulu, New Zealand, Australia and other places. Then she went north through Manila, Hong Kong, and arrived in Shanghai. In the future, she plans to go to Beiping. However, because the war in the north has not subsided, she may not be able to walk to Beiping. After arriving in Beiping, she plans to go to Japan first, and then from South Africa to Europe, visiting various countries. Then she will cross the sea to London to complete this grand tour. While on the road, she plans to write travel books and take films. She has been on the road for two years and expects to reach her goal in another three years.

The Tragic History of the Kidnapping of Famous Actor Liu Yunqing 150

The Cruelty of Bandits in Fujian Province

Nailing Fingers, Gouging Out Eyes, Splitting Skulls

Untying a Belt to Commit Suicide, Finally Rescued

Liu Yunqing, a famous actor from Mazhen, Hubei, is currently 48 years old. He previously performed at the New Stage in Nanshi and then went to perform at the Great Stage in Fuzhou, the provincial capital, for many years. He was known as "Bailingzi" and his reputation spread throughout southern Fujian. His family was originally from his ancestral home. Last spring, he was suddenly kidnapped by bandits who demanded a huge ransom. Because Liu was unable to raise the money, he was subjected to torture in the bandit den for more than a year. Finally, the bandits nailed Liu's ten fingers to the door, gouged out his eyes, split his skull with a knife, and abandoned him in the wilderness. The cruelty of the scene was horrifying. Fortunately, Liu's life was not meant to end, and he was rescued by friends and sent to a nearby hospital for treatment. He was only discharged from the hospital last month. However, Liu is now blind and his ten fingers are broken and incomplete, leaving him disabled. He returned to the Great Stage to sell his belongings to get fare to return home. Unexpectedly, misfortune struck again. The 160 yuan of life-saving money was stolen by a thief on the ship. The ship arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday, and Liu lodged in an inn. He thought that he was useless in the world and decided to commit suicide. Yesterday afternoon at 3 PM, he untied his belt at the Puai Workshop on Wuma Road to commit suicide. Fortunately, Yang Xinzheng, a member of the Caogjing District Municipal Committee, passed by and immediately rescued him. He was not killed. The 1,000 yuan given was to supplement the plaintiff's dowry, which should be deducted from her share of the inheritance in the future and cannot be considered as a received distribution. Subsequently, Judge Zhou announced the conclusion of the debate and that the judgment would be announced at a later date.

Special Article

Rationalization of Industry (Continued from the Third Part) Cheng Zhenjun 164

Of these four steps, the first step is of course the fundamental method, and the first step, the standardization of the company, is something that the company must do for its own benefit. Because without standardization, there can be no mass production; without standardization, there can be no scientific management; without standardization, consumption cannot be eliminated. And mass production, scientific management, and eliminating consumption are all the most beneficial tasks for the company. Therefore, standardization is inseparable from the company. I will now briefly discuss the procedures for standardization within a company. Standardization is closely related to research in the laboratory. For example, the quality of materials, new manufacturing methods, and new inspection methods all come from research. Therefore, to implement standardization, there must be testing. Once there is a testing laboratory, the next step is to draft purchase specifications. All supplies, tools, machines, components, materials, parts, etc., must be specified in detail as the standard for purchase. These specifications are drafted by engineers and must solicit the purchasing department's opinions, because engineers only know the scientific needs, while the purchasing department can consider the market supply situation. In addition to the purchase specifications, there must be inspection specifications. Whether the purchase is made through bidding or other fair methods, after the seller sends the sample, the engineer will begin the inspection according to the inspection specifications to determine whether to accept it. There is often a tolerance limit during this process. If it does not exceed the limit, it can be reluctantly adopted. There are separate inspection specifications for self-manufactured products and must be inspected item by item. As for the standardization of manufacturing methods, it must first be based on the degree of standardization of the equipment before it can be implemented. All letter paper, envelopes, pencils, ink, paper strips, invoices, checks, instructions, etc., must have standards, and standard tools and measuring instruments are fundamental needs in the factory. Because the tools and machines are standardized, and with proper factory layout, continuous manufacturing can be carried out from one level to another, from one method to another. The maximum efficiency of all machines depends on the average speed and orderly methods of manufacturing, so that the interaction between various parts and components has minimal change and minimal resistance, while there is a continuous addition of raw materials, continuous sequential manufacturing, and continuous completion of products. If the equipment is standardized, then the manufacturing methods only need detailed standard instruction manuals to enable workers to understand how to use machines and materials to achieve the desired results, and there must be standard safety rules to prevent workers from any danger. With this, the so-called time study and motion study in scientific management to determine work standards can also have a basis for implementation. The standard of the product is sometimes very difficult to determine and should be based on market research and cost accounting and carefully determined. However, orderers often have purchase specifications to follow. In addition, parts and small items can be standardized. Canned goods, cement, bricks, tiles, nails, doors, and windows are all examples. Some may say that in our country today, the standards of weights and measures set by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce cannot be implemented, so how can we talk about industrial standardization? Little do they know that the standards of weights and measures are one thing, and industrial standardization is another. They can be carried out in parallel without conflict. The standards of weights and measures must be implemented, and there is no reason to wait until the standards of weights and measures are implemented before industrial standardization can be carried out. Moreover, standardization is too important to industry. If our country does not want to revitalize industry, then so be it. But if our country wants to revitalize industry, what other way can it go without standardization? There is another method in rationalization called combination. Combination has two types: horizontal and vertical. Horizontal combination is the combination of an industry with the same industry, such as the combination of the steel industry with the steel industry. Vertical combination is the combination of an industry with related different industries, such as the combination of the steel industry with coal mines and iron mines, or with the machine manufacturing industry. Combination has been practiced in Europe and America for decades and is a feature of modern economic organization. However, the public is quite opposed to it, such as the anti-trust laws in the United States. But in recent years, from experience, it has been gradually realized that combination can make selling prices lower and market conditions more stable, which is indeed beneficial to society. Therefore, the attitude of opposition has changed and tacitly recognizes the need for its existence. For example, the Balfour Committee's 1929 report on industry and commerce in the United Kingdom stated clearly the opinions of the public. The International Economic Conference, organized by labor, capital, and economists, has also included horizontal and vertical combinations in rationalization. It can be seen that combination is a product of industrial development, a worldwide trend that cannot be stopped. I have often traced the reasons for the establishment of combination, and there are three types: (1) The development of machinery. The invention of the steam turbine, the improvement of the engine, the development of the electric motor and the transmission of its high-voltage power, the simplified transportation system and division of labor, and the sufficient standards all enable the work to be expanded and the cost to be reduced. Therefore, the old machines in small factories cannot compete with them and are relegated to the position of elimination. There is no other way except to merge and reorganize to seek survival. (2) The vastness of the market. Large-scale production requires a large-scale market to absorb it. Since the development of railways, highways, sea routes, telegraphs, and telephones, the distance of thousands of miles has been reduced, and transportation and information are extremely convenient. Since the market has become vast, the competition and contact between the same industries have become increasingly apparent. Only through mergers can these be eliminated and the benefits of large-scale production and large-scale distribution be obtained. (3) The emergence of scientific management. With excellent machinery and a vast market, if management is not done properly, mergers will only lead to disputes and will not be beneficial in practice. Therefore, scientific management in the United States has emerged. It does not care about human relationships, but only uses scientific methods to analyze, measure, research, and test to obtain results and implement them. No matter how large or complex the organization is, it is always beneficial. This is also one of the elements that promotes combination. As for the implementation of mergers, valuation methods are often used to jointly estimate the prices of the inventories, machinery, and tools of each party, and then a general management office is organized to direct everything. The staff of this general management office should be selected from the most outstanding talents, and management and machinery should be improved and expanded. Moreover, due to the increase in scale, a testing laboratory can be established for research. These are all advantages of combination that cannot be ignored. In the United States in recent years, the progress of combination has been accelerating, such as public utilities, retail stores and wholesale stores in distribution, banks and financial enterprises, film and game businesses, steel plants, machine plants, manufacturing plants, etc., are too numerous to count. The United Kingdom and Germany also have similar trends. Our country is in the midst of this trend. If we want to develop industry, I am afraid that we cannot be immune. However, there are several things that should be paid attention to when carrying out mergers, which I will record here (1) When various industries are in a state of depression, mergers cannot save them. (2) Mergers cannot salvage the industry in unprofitable years. (3) If the economic organization after the merger is in an unmanageable situation, so that the fixed expenses are greater than the minimum income, then this merger is inappropriate and cannot obtain the benefits of new opportunities, and will undoubtedly fail. (4) The key to merger is good management. I hope that industrialists in our country who adopt mergers will consider these points in advance. In the rationalization carried out in Germany, there is an organization called Cartel, which can be translated as the Industrial Association. The meaning of this is very difficult to determine because the size of its organization and the complexity of its tasks vary with the industry. Now I translate its most approximate definition as [A cartel is an association of producers or distributors that controls market conditions in certain respects.] The control of the market may be solely on production to make the quantity suitable for the elements, so that its price can achieve a satisfactory balance, or it may be strictly regulated solely on the selling price, regardless of the production situation, and production can naturally be limited by the price and the required quantity without the drawback of oversupply, or production and price can be managed simultaneously to make the corresponding supply and demand more secure. Sometimes a whole industry has only one cartel, sometimes the production and price of a whole industry each have a cartel and are all under the management of a general association. Sometimes each part of an industry has a cartel, and there are cooperations and non-cooperations between them. Sometimes many cartels jointly control production and have the right to stipulate how much each factory ships. There is also a central association that stipulates the price for everyone to abide by. The various methods are very different. The purpose of all of them is to eliminate competition, eliminate overproduction, stabilize the market, and obtain high profits. At the same time, in foreign trade, they also increase the strength of business and stand in the best position. Looking at the most developed and most efficient industries in Germany, such as the coal mining industry, the steel industry, and engineering, the organization of cartels in these industries is also the most complete. I will now choose the most complete organization among the cartels as an example to explain it, so that we can know the internal methods. The German Rhine Brown Coal Association (Rheinische BvaunkohlenSynbikat) is in the form of a trading company and has a central sales office. Members, i.e., shareholders, must sign a contract to transfer their produced coal to the sales office. The contract is valid from 1915 to the end of March 1930. The purpose of this cartel is to control the market, control the production and consumption of various mines, and its purpose is to sell coal and allocate the sales components of each mine (Quota). Its nominal capital is 2,122,000 marks, but it does not seek profit itself. Its expenses are paid by collecting ten fenning (one mark is equal to one hundred fenning) for each ton of coal sold to pay it. There is also a compensation fund used to compensate the members' losses, which is also collected in the selling price of coal. If stored, it should not exceed five fenning per ton of briquettes. When voting, the distribution of voting rights is distributed to each member according to the percentage of coal sold, and is modified by the heat value. For example, one ton of briquettes is considered equivalent to two and a half tons of brown coal from the Rhineland (Ｒｈｉｎｅｌａｎｄ) province or two tons of brown coal from the State (Ｓｔａｔｅ) province. There are 26 members in this association (nine belong to government-run companies, eleven belong to mines, and six belong to limited liability companies). The percentage of coal sold is 76.93 for nine members, 12.28 for one member, and 10.9 for six members. Anyone who violates the contract will be heavily fined. The work in the association is divided into four parts (A) Control of production. The role of this association is to make supply and demand correspond to avoid overproduction and price wars. The output of all companies in the association must be handed over to the central agency for distribution according to the prescribed composition. As for technical support in production, each company still handles it independently, but the association provides funding for public research and development. The association has also built 1,230 houses for miners. (B) Control of price sales and market. Selling coal is the exclusive right of this association. All orders from customers are supplied by which company, and the association handles the issuing of invoices, the arranging for shipping to the customer, and the transferring of funds to each company. Moreover, the association decides on the average increase or decrease in the output of each company according to the prescribed components based on market conditions. The components can also be bought and sold, but they must be linked to the designated mine, otherwise they are invalid. Members can request a re-revision of the components every three years. At the end of each year, each member should report the remaining amount that can be supplied outside of the components to the association, so that when demand increases, it can be re-allocated according to the proportional components for supply. The coal used by each company in the association itself is not counted within the components (other associations calculate it separately), that is, the coal used by its affiliated factories, such as chemical plants and steel plants, can also not be counted, but it must be approved by the association, and the so-called affiliated factories must have more than 81% of the shares in the company. The association still has to collect a small amount of fees on all coal that is not counted as components to fill office expenses and prevent fraud. (C) The organization for selling coal has several distribution companies established under the central sales office. Each company has its own sales area, which is delimited according to the location of the railway station. The coal mines near the railway station should be designated to supply the needs of the area. (D) The setting of prices. The association calculates the cost of production in the coal mine, including depreciation, profit, taxes, association expenses, and the income of distributors, and then sets the standard selling price. However, it must be approved by the provincial coal association (Coal Association), and the procedures must be recognized by the provincial government. The price of coal sold by wholesalers should add transportation costs to the standard price at the unloading force. The amount of this increase is regulated by the local coal merchants' association and must allow wholesalers to receive a considerable profit. The above is the method of the Rhine Brown Coal Association. Most other coal industry cartels are similar. Even the cartels of potassium carbonate, cement, and other raw material industries are mostly similar. German law not only allows cartels but also protects them. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce has a cartel court to resolve all disputes. All members of the cartel or the public directly affected can file a complaint against the cartel's contract or resolution, but if the reasons are insufficient, they will be dismissed. The ruling of the court is, in fact, the final ruling. Therefore, the cartels in Germany stand on a solid foundation. However, in recent years, horizontal and vertical combinations have greatly expanded, and cartels are inevitably slightly affected. But the trusts in various countries are now organizing international cartels to control the world market, using scientific methods everywhere. Its success can be established and awaited, but the people of our country are still living in a drunken dream, oblivious to everything, is it not very sad? Compatriots, in this tense state of economic invasion, we should wake up and turn back, resolve to strive on our own, unite our strengths, and be of one mind. I dare to offer two strategies for governing the fundamentals and governing the symptoms. The fundamental cure is to vigorously implement industrial rationalization. The symptomatic cure is to vigorously implement tariff protection policies. The two must be carried out simultaneously and cannot be neglected. In addition, training workers, educating specialists, etc., are all things that should be done in rationalization, and finance, transportation, etc., can also adopt rationalization everywhere to seek their improvement and development. Great is the effect of rationalization! Some say that the result of promoting rationalization in Europe and the United States has caused two problems: one is overproduction and the other is unemployment. So far, there is no solution. Little do they know that these two problems are not the result of rationalization. Rationalization is not responsible for them. Overproduction is known because of the implementation of rationalization. It was not known before. In the past, there were countless products stored in the hands of merchants. Since the implementation of rationalization, direct sales to consumers are often adopted to eliminate the profits of intermediaries and make prices lower. As a result, these remaining items are not scattered in the hands of many merchants but accumulated in the hands of a few factories. No wonder they are all alarmed, thinking that there is overproduction. And simplification, standardization, and scientific management often make the inventory of stores reach the smallest number, so the inventory of factories is even more increased. Therefore, overproduction did not start today, but it is only today that the truth can be fully known through the clear revelation of rationalization, so that production and the market can be properly coordinated, and countless amounts of stagnant capital and its associated consumption can be saved. This is exactly the greatest contribution of rationalization, and it is used to blame it instead. What in the world is more unjust than this? (To be continued)

Weather Report 165

Xujiahui Observatory's meteorological forecast at 4:30 p.m. yesterday stated that it would be hot and cloudy. Along the Shandong coastline and over the Yellow Sea and East Sea, the wind was coming from the north to the east, with increasing force. The weather along the Annam coastline was bad due to a hurricane in the Macclesfield Islands moving northwestward. The hurricane near Guam was also expected to move northwestward. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 p.m. yesterday, the highest temperature in the city was 82.8 degrees and the lowest was 61.7 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 86.0 degrees and the lowest was 63.0 degrees.
